4.9
Summary of results
Busline 150S
OTP - Schedule adherence:
The OTP overall is 73%, 81% for td 1 and 66% for td 2. The average delay is 2.95 min, 1.76
min in td 1 and 4.09 minutes in td 2. The mean for above ﬁve-minute delays is 12.4 (td 1) and
7.7 minutes (td 2) and td 1 shows a high variance for most stops.
OTP - Headway irregularity:
The overall OTP according to MOVIA’s bandwidth for headway regularity is 93%, respectively
94% for td 1 and 93% for td 2. The CoV and PRDM give another impression on the regularity
of the buses. The CoV for td 1 is 0.73 and 0.79 for td 2. The PRDM is 51% for td 1 and 58%
for td 2. The irregularity increases in both tds with the trip distance, which could be due to
the trip distance and/or for td 1 due to the fact that the bus is entering the city and is more
exposed to external factors such as congestion and traﬃc lights.
Trip Time Analysis:
Td 1 has a long dwell time (195 seconds) at ﬁrst stop which causes a delay from the beginning
on and increases in the middle of the route at Venlighedsvej and Dr. Neergaardsvej and can
be partially caught up through driving towards the end of the trip. The delay is especially
inﬂuenced by the journeys in the morning peak. For td 2 delays occur especially in the beginning
of the route in the city (Nørreport St. to Brogårdsvej) and reach up to 6.29 minutes which is
recovered only partially resulting in an average delay of 2.55 minutes at the ﬁnal stop. In both
tds, the morning peak was the main inﬂuence for the delays. Since the average delay from the
origin stop is above 1 minute in both directions an analysis of the layover time in percent of
the run time showed that the shorter the layover time, the higher the average departure delay
at the origin stop.
Dwell time:
The dwell time is in general higher at holding stops than at regular stops. Especially high
is the dwell time in both directions at the corresponding origin stops. The few exceptions of
extremely long dwell times have been investigated and shown to be in the beginning of the
route.
82
==PAGE:94==
Run time:
The average observed and planned run time in td 1 are 54.9, respectively 53.3 minutes. In
general, the run times in the morning (planned and observed) are the longest. In the evening
and night the planned run time is ﬁve minutes lower, compared to the rest of the day. In td
2 the average observed and planned trip time are 53, respectively 51.3 minutes. For td 2 the
observed and planned run time are longer in the afternoon and lower in the evening and night.
Bus bunching:
Bus bunching is happening in 6.63% of all recorded observations for bus line 150S.
Average passenger wait time:
For the high-frequency service between Nørreport St. and Nærum St. the ideal wait time is 2.5
minutes, the actual wait time is 3.56 for td 1 and 3.83 for td 2, resulting in an additional wait
time of 1.06 minutes in td 1 and 1.33 minutes in td 2.
Average passenger travel time:
The ideal and actual passenger travel time for the high-frequency service between Nørreport
St. and Nærum St. is shown per record and the average additional passenger travel time is
0.45 minutes in td 1 and 1.85 minutes in td 2.
Bus line 173E
OTP - Schedule adherence:
The OTP overall is 68%, 70% for td 1 and 67% for td 2. The average delay is 1.97 min, 1.63
min in td 1 and 2.34 minutes in td 2. The mean for above ﬁve-minute delays is 14.3 (td 1) and
10.8 minutes (td 2). The result in td 1 for above ﬁve-minute delays is a high variance for most
stops and high median values, especially at Frederiksborgvej, Forskerparken where the median
value is 18.2 minutes.
OTP - Headway irregularity:
The overall OTP according to MOVIA’s bandwidth for headway regularity is 80%, respectively
83% for td 1 and 77% for td 2. These are worse values than one for bus line 150S but this is
mainly due to the diﬀerence in headways analyzed (10 vs 5 minutes). The CoV and PRDM,
on the other hand, are better compared to the values of the bus line 150S since they are based
on "true" regularity of the buses. The CoV for td 1 is 0.54 and 0.58 for td 2. The PRDM is
83
==PAGE:95==
38% for td 1 and 50% for td 2. The irregularity stays stable until the ﬁnal stop in both tds.
The jump in CoV and PRDM is in td 1 higher than to td 2 which also can be explained by the
entering of the city and more congestion and traﬃc lights.
Trip time analysis:
At td 1 the buses arrive late at the ﬁrst stop, hence they depart delayed by 2.32 minutes. The
delay ﬂuctuates until Nærum St. and decreases towards the ﬁnal stop. For td 1 the morning
peak inﬂuences the last part of the route (in the city) while the afternoon peak inﬂuences the
ﬁrst part of the route. In td 2 the buses start with a departure delay of 0.66 minutes and the
delay increases over distance to 3.87 minutes at the end of the route. Td2 is inﬂuenced by the
morning peak, mainly in the ﬁrst part of the route which is in the city. For the layover analysis
no distinction was made between the bus lines but since also this bus line on average departed
delayed from the origin stop, the results also apply.
Dwell time:
The ﬁndings are similar to the ﬁndings of the bus line 150S, namely that the dwell time is higher
at holding stops than at regular stops. The longest dwell times are seen at the origin stops of
each direction. The few exceptions of extremely long dwell times have been investigated and
shown to be also in the beginning of the route.
Run time:
The average observed and planned run time in td 1 are 43, respectively 44.2 minutes. The
journeys are shorter than planned which is explained through the delayed departure from the
origin stop which is partially recovered along the route and therefore results in a shorter run
time than planned. In general, the run times in the afternoon (planned and observed) are
longer. In td 2 the average observed and planned run time are 37.2, respectively 35 minutes.
For td 2 (unlike in td 1) the planned run time is stable throughout the day but the observed
run time has a "M" shape, where the observed run time is higher than the planned run time in
the morning and afternoon peak, but lower in the early morning, noon and late afternoon.
Bus bunching:
Bus bunching is happening in 2.11% of all recorded observations for bus line 173E.
84
==PAGE:96==
Average passenger wait time:
For the high-frequency service between Nørreport St. and Nærum St. the ideal wait time is 5
minutes, the actual wait time is 6.56 in td 1 and 6.96 for td 2, resulting in an additional wait
time of 1.56 minutes in td 1 and 1.96 minutes in td 2.
Average passenger travel time:
The ideal and actual passenger travel time for the high-frequency service between Nørreport
St. and Nærum St. is shown per record and the average additional passenger travel time is
0.90 minutes in td 1 and 4.87 minutes in td 2.
85
==PAGE:97==
5
Limitations and Conclusion
5.1
Limitations
The limitations of this paper are primarily the limited access to further data, such as passenger
or traﬃc data. With passenger data, one could get a better understanding and interpretation
of the KPIs from the passenger perspective, the average passenger wait and travel time. In this
paper evenly distributed passenger arrival is assumed, though in real life this is not the case.
With passenger data incorporated in the KPIs, the measure would represent the real world, the
"truth", better.
Another limitation is the quality of the data, where 28% of all observations in the used data
set have missing values in either the observed arrival or departure date.
Also the timeliness of the data is another limitation for the interpretation of the results. Since
2014 minor changes have already been applied, such as the renaming of bus lines or the tem-
porary re-routing of stops.
Regarding bus bunching there was no data on the bus stop size or length and therefore it was
assumed that all bus stops only allowed one bus at a time to stop for boarding and alighting
of passengers. This, however, is not true, since especially in the city center bus stops allow
the stopping of multiple buses. In this research, the bus stop size was adjusted to the best of
knowledge but a complete and correct picture of all bus stops is not given.
86
==PAGE:98==
5.2
Conclusion
In this chapter conclusions of the study and recommendations for future research are presented.
The main objective of this paper was to analyze the punctuality and reliability of public bus
transportation in Greater Copenhagen. Two representative bus lines, 150S and the 173E have
been chosen and evaluated using diﬀerent performance measures. Data used in the analysis
was obtained from the AVL by MOVIA. Six reliability indicators that reﬂect the interests of
both public transportation operators and passengers are applied. These indicators are OTP
in terms of schedule adherence and headway irregularity, run time variability, bus bunching,
passenger waiting time and passenger travel time. The ﬁrst four of the indicators reﬂect the
reliability of the public transportation perspective and the last two indicators represent the
passenger’s perspective of reliability. Furthermore, trip analysis along stops and the dwell time
were analyzed to better understand the reasons and causes for irregularity along the route.
OTP - schedule adherence:
The KPI for schedule adherence benchmarks compared to other international cities in the
middle, still, it is below its target value. In order to optimize the schedule adherence, several
actions can be initiated. Driver training and inspection or schedule optimization could be two
initiatives. For example for bus 173E in td 2 the schedule could be optimized for the bus
stop Brogårdsvej and onwards, since there is a jump in delay which is then carried until the
end of the route. Further research could be done by developing and conﬁguring a dynamic
programming algorithm for optimizing the bus schedule similar to Chen [2014]. The algorithm
optimizes the number of buses and departure times according to the passenger demand.
OTP - headway regularity (and bus bunching):
For both bus lines the regularity measures did not show great results. In order to improve the
headway regularity and bus bunching a headway-based indicator could be introduced. This
indicator is installed in the bus and communicates to the bus driver real-time data from the
bus ahead and behind. Through this indicator, the bus driver knows if he is too close to the
bus in front or to the bus behind and can thereupon adjust the speed or hold at a bus stop.
This is similar to the method applied in the ﬁeld study of Cats [2014] and could be improved
even further when applying the a family of dynamic holding strategies like suggested by Xuan
87
==PAGE:99==
et al. [2011].
Trip analysis along the route:
For both bus lines the phenomena is seen that the td 1 is performing better than the td 2. This
is because of two reasons. Firstly because the scheduled run times are shorter for td 2 than for
td1. Secondly because the delay mainly occurs due to the part of the route in the city center.
In td 1 the part through the city center is at the end of the route, hence the overall delay occurs
mainly there, while for td 2 the delay from the city center occurs right in the beginning and
is carried throughout the whole trip and not (or only partially) being recovered. In order to
decrease the delay occurring in the city further introduction of infrastructural changes such as
more traﬃc signal priorities at intersections could help to improve performance. A simulation
could be applied to discover the beneﬁts of such measures.
Furthermore, for bus line 173E in td2 a schedule optimization is suggested in order to not have
the high variance in delay in the beginning of the route.
Interestingly both bus lines depart delayed from the origin station and the analysis of layover
in percent of run time showed that 70% of the buses have a layover time of under 50% of their
planned run time. Furthermore, the analysis showed that with a minimum layover time of 10%
of the run time, an improvement or decrease in delays of 13% can be achieved. Therefore it
is suggested to adjust the minimum layover time to 10% and to instruct bus drivers to arrive
earlier in order to depart on time.
Dwell time:
The dwell time analysis showed that the dwell time at holding stops was higher than at regular
stops. It is not a huge diﬀerence, therefore, the optimization of the holding strategy would
only improve the overall performance slightly. However the optimization of layover time could
improve the extremely long dwell times in the beginning of the route.
Run time:
Diﬀerent run times depending on the hour of the day and td are mostly already incorporated
in the schedule. For bus line 173E in td 2 it is not yet the case, despite diﬀerent observed run
times, depending on the peak of the day. This suggests that the schedule can be optimized
and conﬁgured ﬂexible similar to td 1. Furthermore, the run times can be improved in order to
improve KPIs such as OTP and passenger wait and travel time. An evaluation of the ideal run
88
==PAGE:100==
time through an analysis like in Van Oort [2011] is recommended. In the analysis of Van Oort
[2011] in The Hague, an optimal run time was found to be the 35th percentile of observed run
times and minimized the average total travel time per passenger. It should be noted that the
lower the chosen percentile, the higher the layover time should be to ensure OTP at the origin
stop.
Passenger wait time:
Headway variability is the main cause of variability in wait time for high-frequency bus lines.
Improving headway irregularity, as suggested above, would minimize passenger wait times.
Passenger travel time:
Passenger travel time in this paper consist of waiting time and run time. The suggestions for
improvements for these two measures will automatically minimize additional passenger travel
time.
Concluding, it can be said that this paper provides a detailed analysis about the punctuality
and reliability of public bus transport of the bus line 150S and 173E in Greater Copenhagen,
draws conclusions and presents recommendations for future research.
89

• Data cleaning:
– Delete journeys with only one or two valid observations (timestamp is NULL), since
a wrong log in by the bus driver or an error in the AVL can be assumed
– Timestamp check: Delete the journey if the departure at a stop is before the arrival
– Timestamp check: Delete the journey if the stop has an earlier time stamp than one
of the previous stops
